**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

## 1. Executive Branch Leadership & Actions

### 1.1 Presidential Foreign Engagements
President Trump has established clear conditions in Middle East negotiations, telling Gulf leaders that Iran must cease support for proxy groups before any nuclear deal can proceed [1]. The administration's stance on Qatar shows marked evolution—despite Trump labeling Qatar "funders of terrorism" in 2017 [2], he recently compared a luxury aircraft gift from the country to the historical significance of the Statue of Liberty [3]. International institutions are actively recruiting American researchers who are described as "shunned" under current administration policies [4].

### 1.2 Presidential Ethics & Controversies
Multiple ethics concerns surround the administration, with particular focus on cryptocurrency interests. CNN reports that "Trump's crypto conflicts keep piling up. He's not even trying to hide them" [1]. A Bloomberg report indicates a cryptocurrency speculator claims access to a presidential dinner for just $1,200 [2], while a Chinese-connected company reportedly plans to purchase $300 million in Trump's cryptocurrency [3]. Reports suggest some form of arrangement between Trump and a Mexican cartel leader, described as a "stunning deal" [4]. Senator Sanders has characterized Trump's science policies as "an attack against anyone who has ever loved someone with cancer" [5].

### 1.3 Presidential Communications & Rhetoric
The President has articulated a clear welfare policy stance: "If you want welfare and can work, you must" [1]. His economic messaging has included unusual appeals for Americans to reduce consumption [2]. Trump responded forcefully to criticism over the Qatar jet gift, with The New Republic describing him as "fully losing it" over the pushback [3]. In comments about Senate Majority Leader Chuck Schumer, Trump reportedly said he "has become a Palestinian" [4]. During a speech in Saudi Arabia, where homosexuality is punishable by death, Trump notably played what's described as a "gay anthem" at the close [5].

## 2. Government Efficiency & Restructuring

### 2.1 DOGE Performance & Leadership Issues
Six months after its establishment, Elon Musk's Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE) faces critical evaluation. Financial analysis shows the department has "yet to find a fraction of the hoped for savings" [1], with reports that it is "falling spectacularly short" of targets [2]. Questions of conflicts of interest have emerged, with reporting that a Musk adviser "may make as much as $1 million a year while helping to dismantle" agencies that regulate Musk's own companies [3]. The Verge reports that "Musk's apparent power play at the Copyright Office completely backfired" [4].

### 2.2 Administrative Reform & Workforce Impact
The Trump administration's approach to bureaucratic restructuring has elicited mixed assessments. The Hill published an opinion piece supporting the President's vision, stating "the administrative state needs a reset" [1], while MSNBC characterizes the administration's organizational structure as "impossible" and exposing "a key weakness" [2]. Federal employees affected by DOGE-initiated workforce reductions continue organized resistance, with terminated workers gathering "in Capitol for 10th time" to urge Congress to reverse the cuts [3].

[1] Trump is right: The administrative state needs a reset, https://thehill.com/opinion/white-house/5298323-trump-is-right-the-administrative-state-needs-a-reset/

## 3. International Relations & Trade

### 3.1 Middle East Policy & Security
U.S. Middle East policy shows significant shifts in key relationships. The New York Times published an opinion piece arguing that "This Israeli Government Is Not Our Ally" [1], while reporting documents Israeli military operations in Gaza causing dozens of civilian casualties, "including at least 22 children" [2]. Simultaneously, the administration has negotiated a "$142B Arms Deal" with Saudi Arabia while meeting Syria's new leadership and removing previously imposed sanctions [3]. Despite ongoing Gaza casualties, the administration appears to be discouraging Israeli military action against Iran while pursuing dialogue with Tehran [4]. Domestic security concerns continue with the arrest of a "Former National Guardsman" for an "ISIS Terror Attack Plot on Army Base" [5].

### 3.2 Trade Policies & Global Partnerships
The administration's tariff policies have produced varied outcomes across different trade relationships. Canada's retaliatory tariffs against U.S. goods have reportedly declined to "nearly zero" due to extensive exemptions [1], while domestic economic impacts of Trump's tariffs have been "little impact on prices so far, defying grim forecasts" [2]. In the technology sector, Nvidia has successfully lobbied for "reversal of AI chip limits" while supporting restrictions on Chinese competitor Huawei [3]. A significant revelation regarding U.S. security infrastructure abroad has emerged with reporting on a long-concealed "U.S. Nuclear Base Hidden Under Greenland's Ice for Decades" [4].

[1] Canada's New Tariffs on US Drop to 'Nearly Zero' With Exemptions, Oxford Says, https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2025-05-14/canada-s-new-tariffs-on-us-drop-to-nearly-zero-with-exemptions-oxford-says

[3] Nvidia's flattery of Trump wins reversal of AI chip limits and a Huawei clampdown | ﻿Obstacles threatening Nvidia's AI chip dominance are being tactically removed., https://www.theverge.com/news/666605/nvidias-flattery-of-trump-wins-reversal-of-ai-chip-limits-and-a-huawei-clampdown

## 4. Immigration & Border Security

### 4.1 Citizenship & Border Policies
The Supreme Court is currently considering a Trump administration order that could significantly impact birthright citizenship, creating uncertainty for immigrants like a "Pregnant Cuban immigrant" concerned about her unborn child's legal status [1]. In a separate development, The New York Times reports that "Cartel Family Members Cross Border in Apparent Deal With U.S." according to an unnamed official [2]. The administration's asylum policies have generated controversy, particularly regarding South African refugees, with the Episcopal Church stating it "won't help Trump resettle White South Africans" [3], while South African President Ramaphosa has characterized "Afrikaners granted asylum in US" as "cowards" [4].

Immigration enforcement has intensified in specific sectors, with ICE targeting "Hawaii's prized Kona fields" [1]. A newly unsealed agreement between ICE and the IRS has raised concerns about compromising "sensitive taxpayer data of millions" [2], while community protection networks have formed in some regions to shield residents from immigration raids [3].

## 5. Healthcare & Public Health

### 5.1 Healthcare Access & Regulations
California Governor Gavin Newsom has proposed significant restrictions to healthcare programs for undocumented immigrants, including freezing Medi-Cal enrollment for adults lacking legal status and implementing new premiums to "save more than $5 billion" [1]. In a major regulatory shift, the "FDA Moves to Take Fluoride Supplements for Children Off the Market" [2], though specific scientific or safety concerns motivating this decision are not elaborated in available reporting.

### 5.2 HHS Leadership & Vaccine Policies
Health and Human Services Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. faces increased congressional scrutiny, with scheduled appearances before the Senate health committee described as his "first time since he was confirmed" [1]. On vaccine policy, Kennedy has made statements distancing himself from providing guidance, acknowledging that "I don't think people should be taking medical advice from me" [2]. The administration's public health initiatives have generated confusion, with reports that the "Trump administration's universal flu vaccine project puzzles scientists" [3].
